Slave's Debt and Indication of Permission: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Expands ruling that slave's transactions indicate master's permission for debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi fiqh uses istihsan to validate a slave's debt transactions based on apparent permission, and distinguish this from the qiyas-based ruling.

Core Idea
A slave's public trading is sufficient evidence of permission, overriding qiyas-based doubt.

In Hanafi fiqh, the transaction of a slave raises an important question: can he be sold for debts incurred through trade? While strict analogy (qiyas) would require explicit proof of the master's permission, juristic preference (istihsan) considers the slave's active engagement in trade as sufficient evidence. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi preference for istihsan to avoid hardship and ensure commercial stability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
A slave trades and incurs debt. Creditors seek payment from the slave's sale. The key issue is whether the master permitted the trade.
2
State the qiyas argument
Under qiyas, since the slave could be either authorized (ma'dhun) or interdicted (mahjur), permission is not established by doubt. Hence, the slave cannot be sold for debt because the property is the master's.
3
Explain the istihsan argument
Istihsan holds that the slave's public buying and selling is evidence of permission, because a rational adult would not engage in invalid transactions. This avoids hardship and chaos in commerce.
4
Analyze the burden of proof
If the master acknowledges permission, the slave is sold for debt. If the master claims interdiction, his word is accepted (default ownership), and creditors must provide evidence.
5
Draw the practical conclusion
The mufta bihi position is that the slave can be sued for debts based on his actions indicating permission, following istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا إن سكت عن الإذن والحجر فإنَّ تصرُّفَهُ دليل على إذنه، (ولا يباع لدينه إلا إذا أقر سيده " بإذنه ) ؛ لأنَّ المولى إذا لم يقرّ بالإذن، فالدين لا يظهر في حقه، والمعاملون إنما تضرروا لأنهم اعتمدوا على ظاهر الحال ، والمولى لم يغرَّهم و[؟] قلنا : إن قولهم لا يقبل لضاق الأمر على النّاس ؛ لأنه حينئذ يحتاج العبد إلى أن يستصحب مولاه آناء الليل وأطراف النهار، أو شاهدين عادلين يشهدان على الإذن والمضاربة، وما ضاق أمراه إذ اتّسع فيه. كذا في «حاشية الجلبي » ناقلا عن «البيانية». [١] قوله : دليل على إذنه ؛ والقياس أنه لا يجوز بيعه وشراؤه ؛ لأنه يحتمل أن يكون مأذوناً أو محجوراً، فلا يثبت الإذن بالشك، وما في يده مال لمولاه، فلا يباع في دينه بالشك. وفي الاستحسان: يجوز أن يطالب العبد بديون الغرماء ؛ لأنّ إقدامه على المبايعة مع الناس دليل على إقراره أنه مأذون ؛ لأنه عاقل دين، فالظاهر أنه لا يقدم على تصرفات باطلة. كذا في «حاشية الجلبي» ناقلا عن «البيانية». [٢] قوله : إلا إذا أقرّ سيده ؛ أي يقول المولى : إنّه مأذون ؛ فإنه يباع حينئذ فإنّ حكم المأذون أن يباع في الدين، وأما إن قال إنّه محجورٌ فالقول قوله ؛ لأنه متمسك بالأصل، وعلى الغرماء البيِّنة ؛ لأنَّ دعوى العبدِ الإذن كدعوى الإعتاق والكتابة فلا يقبل قوله عند جحود[؟] المولى إلا بالبينة. كذا في «حاشية الجلبي» [٣] قوله : والمولى لم يغرهم ؛ أي لم يجعلهم مغروراً.
And similarly if he is silent about permission and interdiction, then his transaction is evidence of his permission. (And he is not sold for his debt unless his master acknowledges permission) because if the master does not acknowledge permission, the debt is not established against him, and the creditors only suffered because they relied on the apparent situation, and the master did not deceive them. And we say: Their statement is not accepted, for if it were, it would make matters difficult for people because then the slave would need to bring his master at all times of night and day, or two just witnesses to testify to permission and mudarabah, and his matter would become difficult while it was spacious. Thus in 'Hashiyat al-Jalabi' quoting from 'al-Biyaniyyah'. [1] His statement: 'evidence of his permission'; and by qiyas it is not permissible to sell or buy from him because he could be authorized or interdicted, so permission is not established by doubt, and what is in his hand is the property of his master, so he is not sold for his debt due to doubt. And by istihsan: it is permissible to demand payment from the slave for the debts of creditors because his engaging in transactions with people is evidence of his admission that he is authorized, for he is a rational adult, and it is apparent that he would not engage in invalid transactions. Thus in 'Hashiyat al-Jalabi' quoting from 'al-Biyaniyyah'. [2] His statement: 'unless his master acknowledges'; meaning the master says he is authorized; then he is sold at that time, for the ruling of the authorized is that he is sold for debt. And if he says he is interdicted, then his statement is accepted because he is adhering to the original principle, and the burden of proof is on the creditors, because the slave's claim of authorization is like a claim of emancipation or kitabah, so his statement is not accepted when the master denies except with evidence. Thus in 'Hashiyat al-Jalabi'. [3] His statement: 'and the master did not deceive them'; meaning he did not make them deceived.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling that a slave is not sold for his debts unless his master acknowledges his permission to trade. The commentary first states that if the master remains silent about permission and interdiction, the slave's active trading is taken as evidence of permission. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to avoid hardship, as requiring explicit proof of permission would be impractical. The passage then contrasts qiyas (strict analogy), which would require explicit permission because of doubt, with istihsan, which considers the slave's actions as sufficient proof due to the reasonable assumption that a rational adult would not engage in invalid transactions. If the master acknowledges permission, the slave is sold for debt. If the master claims interdiction, his word is accepted because the default is the master's ownership, and the creditors must provide evidence. The mention of 'emancipation and kitabah' indicates that the slave's claim of authorization is treated similarly: it requires evidence. The commentary concludes by clarifying that the master did not deceive the creditors; they relied on the apparent situation.

Key Terms
مأذون (ma'dhun): A slave who is permitted by his master to engage in trade, as indicated by his actions or explicit permission.
محجور (mahjur): A slave who is interdicted and not permitted to trade; his transactions are invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The transaction is invalid because permission is not established.
B) The slave can be sued for debts because his actions indicate permission.
C) The master must explicitly acknowledge permission for the debt to be collectible.
D) The creditors must bring witnesses to prove permission.

Key Takeaway
A slave's transactions indicate his master's permission by istihsan, allowing creditors to seek repayment from the slave's sale.

Condition of Understanding and Guardian Hierarchy for Authorizing a Minor
States condition of understanding and guardian hierarchy for authorized minor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the cognitive condition required for a minor to be authorized to trade and list the guardian hierarchy according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The minor must understand that sale transfers ownership; only the father, his executor, grandfather, or judge may authorize.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya establishes the fundamental prerequisites for a minor to be granted trade permission. It specifies that mere verbal ability is insufficient; the minor must comprehend the legal effect of the transaction. Furthermore, it delineates a strict hierarchy of guardians who can grant such authorization, excluding relatives like the mother or uncle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cognitive condition
The minor must understand that sale removes ownership and purchase brings ownership. This is a conceptual understanding, not just knowledge of words.
This condition ensures the minor can assess benefit and harm in trade.
2
List the guardian hierarchy
The guardians who can authorize, in order: father, his appointed executor (after death), grandfather, his executor, then the judge or his executor.
The executor is appointed after death; an agent appointed during life is not an executor.
3
Note exclusions
The mother, uncle, and other relatives are not among the guardians who can authorize trade for the minor.
The same rule applies to a mentally incompetent person (ma'tuh) who understands sale.

وشرطه : أن يعقل البيع سالباً للملك والشراء جالباً له. ووليه : أبوه، ثم وصيه، ثم جده ثم وصيه. ولنا : إنّ التصرف المشروع صدرَ من أهله في محله عن ولاية شرعية، فوجب تنفيذه على ما عرف تقريره في الخلافيات، والصبا سبب الحجر؛ لعدم الهداية لا لذاته، وقد ثبتت نظراً إلى إذن الولي وبقاء ولايته لنظر الصبي؛ لاستيفاء المصلحة بطريقين، واحتمال تبدل الحال، بخلاف الطلاق والعتاق؛ لأنه ضار محض، فلم يؤهل له. والنافع المحض، كقبول الهبة والصدقة يؤهل له قبل الإذن، والبيع والشراء دائر بين النفع والضرر، فيجعل أهلاً له بعد الإذن لا قبله، لكن قبل الإذن يكون موقوفاً منه على إجازة الولي؛ لاحتمال وقوعه نظراً للصبي، وصحة التصرف في نفسه. قوله : وشرطه؛ أي شرط كونه مأذوناً يعني أن الشرط من كون الصبي عاقلاً أن يعرف مضمون البيع والشراء، لا أن يعرف مجرّد العبارة. قوله : ووليه أبوه؛ أي الصبي ثم وصي الأب بعد موته، ثم وصي وصيه، ثمّ بعدهم جـده الصحيح وإن عــلا، ثـم بـعـد مــوت الجـد وصـيه، ثم وصــي وصيه. «القُهستاني». وزاد هو والزيلعي : ثم الوالي بالطريق الأولى، ثم القاضي أو وصيه. كذا في «الدر المختار»، قال في «الهندية»: المعتوه الذي يعقلُ البيع يأذن له الأب والوصي والجد دون الأخ والعم، وحكمه حكم الصبي. انتهى. ثم القاضي أو وصيه: إنما قال : ثم وصيه في الأولين، وقال : أو وصيه في الأخير؛ لأنّ وصي الأبِ من استخلفَهُ بعد موتِهِ في التصرف في مال ولده، وأما الذي أذن له في التّصرُّفِ حالَ حياتِهِ فوكيل لا وصي، وكذا في الجد، وأما وصي القاضي فهو الذي أمره بالتّصرف في مال اليتيم، فهو يتصرف في حال حياة القاضي، وإنما سمي وصيَّاً مع أنَّ الإيصاء هو الاستخلاف بعد الموت؛ لأنَّ هنا يصير خليفة للأب، كان الأب جعله وصيّاً، فإن فعل القاضي يصير كفعله، فمعنى الكلام أن وليه أبوه، ثم وصيه بعد موته، ثم الجد إن لم يكن الأب، ولا وصيه ثم وصيه بعد موته، ثمَّ القاضي أو وصيه، أيهما تصرف صح. ( ولو أقر بما معه من كسبه أو إرثه صح، فإنَّ المولى إذا أذنَ الصَّبي بالتجارة صح إقراره بكسبه؛ لأنَّه من تمام التجارة، إذ لو لم يصح إقرارُهُ لا يعاملُهُ النَّاسُ، مع أن إقرار الولي لا يصح؛ لأنه إقرار على الغير، وإقرار الصبي إقرار على نفسه. وقال في «رد المحتار»: ثم حكم المعتوه حكم الصبي إذا بلغ معتوهاً، أما إذا بلغ عاقلاً ثم عَته لا تعود الولاية إلى الأب قياساً، بل إلى القاضي أو السلطان، وفي الاستحسان: تعود إليه، قيل: الأول قول أبي يوسف، والثاني قول محمد، وقيل: الأول قول زفر، والثاني قول علمائنا الثلاثة. كما في «التاتارخانية». [١]قوله : ثم القاضي أو وصيه...الخ، أما الأم أو وصيّ الأم فلا يصح منهم الإذن له في التجارة؛ لأنه غير ولي في التصرفات مطلقاً، بل هو كالأجنبي إلا فيما يرجع إلى حفظه؛ ولهذا لا يملك بيع عقاره، وإنّما جازَ بيع وصي الأم العروض التي ورثها الصغير من الأم بطريق التحصين، والحفظ على الأم الميتة، وعلى الصغير لا لأنه تجارة، حتى لو اشترى شيئاً آخر لليتيم لا يجوز، وليس في الإذن تحصين وحفظ. كذا في «الكفاية»(۲). [۲]قوله : صح إقراره بكسبه؛ عيناً كان أو ديناً لوليه أو لغيره. (۳) قوله : مع أن إقرار الولي لا يصح... الخ؛ إشارة إلى ما عسى يرد على قوله
Its condition: that he understand the sale as removing ownership and the purchase as bringing ownership. His guardian: his father, then his executor, then his grandfather, then his executor. Our proof: The permissible transaction issued from its people in its place with legitimate guardianship, so its execution is obligatory according to what was established in the disputations. Minorhood is a cause for restriction due to lack of guidance, not in its essence, and it is established regarding the permission of the guardian and the continuation of his guardianship for the minor's benefit by two ways, and the possibility of a change of circumstances, unlike divorce and manumission because they are pure harm, so he is not qualified for them. Pure benefit, like accepting a gift or charity, qualifies him before permission, but sale and purchase oscillate between benefit and harm, so he is made qualified for them after permission, not before, but before permission they are suspended pending the guardian's approval due to the possibility of it occurring for the minor's benefit, and the transaction's validity in itself. He said: 'Its condition' i.e. the condition of being authorized means that the condition of the minor being sane is that he know the meaning of sale and purchase, not just the mere wording. He said: 'His guardian is his father' i.e. the minor, then the father's executor after his death, then the executor's executor, then after them the sound grandfather even if elevated, then after the grandfather's death his executor, then his executor's executor. Al-Qahistani added: then the ruler by first right, then the judge or his executor. From al-Durr al-Mukhtar: The insane person who understands sale is permitted by the father, executor, and grandfather, not the brother or uncle, and his ruling is the ruling of the minor. Then the judge or his executor: He only said 'his executor' in the first two, and 'his executor' in the last because the father's executor is the one he appointed after his death to dispose of his son's wealth, whereas the one who permitted him to dispose during his life is an agent, not an executor, and similarly for the grandfather. The judge's executor is the one he ordered to dispose of the orphan's wealth, so he disposes during the judge's life, and he is called an executor even though executorship is succession after death, because here he becomes the father's successor, as if the father made him an executor, so what the judge does becomes as if he did it. So the meaning is: his guardian is his father, then his executor after his death, then the grandfather if the father and his executor are absent, then his executor after his death, then the judge or his executor, whichever disposed is valid. And if he acknowledges regarding his earnings or inheritance with him, it is valid, because when the master permits the minor to trade, his acknowledgment of his earnings is valid because it is part of trade, since if his acknowledgment were not valid, people would not deal with him, even though the guardian's acknowledgment is not valid, because it is an acknowledgment on behalf of another, and the minor's acknowledgment is an acknowledgment against himself. And in Radd al-Muhtar: The ruling of the insane is the ruling of the minor if he reached puberty insane, but if he reached puberty sane then became insane, guardianship does not return to the father by analogy, but to the judge or ruler, and in istihsan: it returns to him. It is said: the first is Abu Yusuf's view, and the second is Muhammad's view, and it is said: the first is Zufar's view, and the second is the view of our three imams. As in al-Tatarkhaniyya. He said: Then the judge or his executor... etc. As for the mother or the mother's executor, they cannot permit him to trade because they are not guardians in transactions absolutely, but are like strangers except regarding preservation; for this reason he does not own the sale of his real estate, and the sale of the mother's executor of the goods that the minor inherited from the mother is permitted by way of strengthening and preservation for the deceased mother, and for the minor, not because it is trade, so if he buys something else for the orphan it is not permissible, and there is no strengthening or preservation in permission. From al-Kifaya. He said: His acknowledgment of his earnings is valid, whether it is an asset or a debt to his guardian or others. He said: Even though the guardian's acknowledgment is not valid... etc.; an indication of what might be objected to his statement.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is an expansion on the conditions and guardianship for a minor to be authorized (ma'dhun) for trade. The author first states the condition: the minor must be capable of understanding that sale removes ownership and purchase brings it. This is a cognitive condition, not merely knowing words. Then the hierarchy of guardians who can grant permission is given: father, his executor, grandfather, his executor, then the judge or his executor. The commentary clarifies that the 'executor' of the father is appointed after death, while a person authorized during life is an agent. For the judge, his 'executor' acts under his authority during his life. The text then presents a proof (lana) that the minor can be authorized because the transaction issues from a capable person with legitimate guardianship, and minorhood is a restriction due to lack of guidance, not an inherent bar. Permission and continuing guardianship allow for benefit. Divorce and manumission are pure harm, so not permitted. Pure benefit (like accepting gifts) is permitted before permission. Sale and purchase are mixed, so only after permission, though prior transactions are suspended. Next, the ruling on acknowledgment: if a minor acknowledges debt or property related to his trade earnings or inheritance, it is valid. This is necessary for trade to function; otherwise people would not deal with him. The guardian's acknowledgment is invalid because it is on behalf of another. The passage ends with an intra-Hanafi dispute: if a person reaches puberty sane then becomes insane, does guardianship return to the father? By analogy (qiyas) it goes to the judge; by istihsan it returns to the father. This is reported as a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, or between Zufar and the three imams. The mufta bihi position is not explicitly given here, but later texts may prefer the istihsan view. This passage exemplifies the Hanafi method of combining logical deduction (qiyas) with preference (istihsan) and the importance of understanding (ta'qul) for legal capacity.

Key Terms
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): A minor who is authorized by a guardian to engage in trade.
الولي (al-wali): The guardian empowered to authorize the minor for trade, specifically father, his executor, grandfather, his executor, judge or his executor.
الإذن (al-idhn): Permission granted by a guardian to a minor to engage in trade, making his transactions effective after permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The father
B) The mother
C) The grandfather
D) The judge

Key Takeaway
A minor can be authorized to trade if he understands the legal effect of sale and purchase, and the authorization must come from a specific guardian: father, executor, grandfather, or judge.

Proof, Acknowledgment, and Dispute on Guardianship for Authorized Minor
States proof, acknowledgment ruling, and intra-Hanafi dispute on guardianship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi proof for authorizing a minor to trade, state the validity of the minor's acknowledgment, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on return of guardianship after insanity.

Core Idea
The minor's authorized transaction is valid because it issues from a capable person with lawful guardianship; his acknowledgment binds him, but guardianship return is disputed.

This lesson delves into the rational proof (dalil aqli) that supports authorizing a minor, the distinction between pure benefit, pure harm, and mixed transactions, and the important ruling on acknowledgment. It also examines an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: if a person who reached puberty sane later becomes insane, does guardianship return to the father or go to the judge?

Guided Path
1
Understand the proof (lana)
The proof states that a permissible transaction from a capable person with lawful guardianship must be executed. Minorhood is a restriction due to lack of guidance, not inherent incapacity.
This is a rational argument (qiyas) based on maslaha.
2
Distinguish transaction types
Pure harm (divorce, manumission) is not permitted for a minor. Pure benefit (accepting gifts) is permitted even without permission. Mixed benefit and harm (sale, purchase) requires permission.
Before permission, the minor's transaction is suspended (mawquf) pending guardian approval.
3
Recognize the ruling on acknowledgment
If an authorized minor acknowledges a debt or property related to his trade earnings or inheritance, it is valid. This is necessary for trade to function.
The guardian's acknowledgment is invalid because it is on behalf of another, while the minor's is on himself.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
If a person reaches puberty sane then becomes insane, guardianship does not return to the father by qiyas (Abu Yusuf, Zufar), but by istihsan it returns to the father (Muhammad, three imams).
The mufta bihi position leans toward istihsan in later texts.

وشرطه : أن يعقل البيع سالباً للملك والشراء جالباً له. ووليه : أبوه، ثم وصيه، ثم جده ثم وصيه. ولنا : إنّ التصرف المشروع صدرَ من أهله في محله عن ولاية شرعية، فوجب تنفيذه على ما عرف تقريره في الخلافيات، والصبا سبب الحجر؛ لعدم الهداية لا لذاته، وقد ثبتت نظراً إلى إذن الولي وبقاء ولايته لنظر الصبي؛ لاستيفاء المصلحة بطريقين، واحتمال تبدل الحال، بخلاف الطلاق والعتاق؛ لأنه ضار محض، فلم يؤهل له. والنافع المحض، كقبول الهبة والصدقة يؤهل له قبل الإذن، والبيع والشراء دائر بين النفع والضرر، فيجعل أهلاً له بعد الإذن لا قبله، لكن قبل الإذن يكون موقوفاً منه على إجازة الولي؛ لاحتمال وقوعه نظراً للصبي، وصحة التصرف في نفسه. قوله : وشرطه؛ أي شرط كونه مأذوناً يعني أن الشرط من كون الصبي عاقلاً أن يعرف مضمون البيع والشراء، لا أن يعرف مجرّد العبارة. قوله : ووليه أبوه؛ أي الصبي ثم وصي الأب بعد موته، ثم وصي وصيه، ثمّ بعدهم جـده الصحيح وإن عــلا، ثـم بـعـد مــوت الجـد وصـيه، ثم وصــي وصيه. «القُهستاني». وزاد هو والزيلعي : ثم الوالي بالطريق الأولى، ثم القاضي أو وصيه. كذا في «الدر المختار»، قال في «الهندية»: المعتوه الذي يعقلُ البيع يأذن له الأب والوصي والجد دون الأخ والعم، وحكمه حكم الصبي. انتهى. ثم القاضي أو وصيه: إنما قال : ثم وصيه في الأولين، وقال : أو وصيه في الأخير؛ لأنّ وصي الأبِ من استخلفَهُ بعد موتِهِ في التصرف في مال ولده، وأما الذي أذن له في التّصرُّفِ حالَ حياتِهِ فوكيل لا وصي، وكذا في الجد، وأما وصي القاضي فهو الذي أمره بالتّصرف في مال اليتيم، فهو يتصرف في حال حياة القاضي، وإنما سمي وصيَّاً مع أنَّ الإيصاء هو الاستخلاف بعد الموت؛ لأنَّ هنا يصير خليفة للأب، كان الأب جعله وصيّاً، فإن فعل القاضي يصير كفعله، فمعنى الكلام أن وليه أبوه، ثم وصيه بعد موته، ثم الجد إن لم يكن الأب، ولا وصيه ثم وصيه بعد موته، ثمَّ القاضي أو وصيه، أيهما تصرف صح. ( ولو أقر بما معه من كسبه أو إرثه صح، فإنَّ المولى إذا أذنَ الصَّبي بالتجارة صح إقراره بكسبه؛ لأنَّه من تمام التجارة، إذ لو لم يصح إقرارُهُ لا يعاملُهُ النَّاسُ، مع أن إقرار الولي لا يصح؛ لأنه إقرار على الغير، وإقرار الصبي إقرار على نفسه. وقال في «رد المحتار»: ثم حكم المعتوه حكم الصبي إذا بلغ معتوهاً، أما إذا بلغ عاقلاً ثم عَته لا تعود الولاية إلى الأب قياساً، بل إلى القاضي أو السلطان، وفي الاستحسان: تعود إليه، قيل: الأول قول أبي يوسف، والثاني قول محمد، وقيل: الأول قول زفر، والثاني قول علمائنا الثلاثة. كما في «التاتارخانية». Its condition: that he understand the sale as removing ownership and the purchase as bringing ownership. His guardian: his father, then his executor, then his grandfather, then his executor. Our proof: The permissible transaction issued from its people in its place with legitimate guardianship, so its execution is obligatory according to what was established in the disputations. Minorhood is a cause for restriction due to lack of guidance, not in its essence, and it is established regarding the permission of the guardian and the continuation of his guardianship for the minor's benefit by two ways, and the possibility of a change of circumstances, unlike divorce and manumission because they are pure harm, so he is not qualified for them. Pure benefit, like accepting a gift or charity, qualifies him before permission, but sale and purchase oscillate between benefit and harm, so he is made qualified for them after permission, not before, but before permission they are suspended pending the guardian's approval due to the possibility of it occurring for the minor's benefit, and the transaction's validity in itself. He said: 'Its condition' i.e. the condition of being authorized means that the condition of the minor being sane is that he know the meaning of sale and purchase, not just the mere wording. He said: 'His guardian is his father' i.e. the minor, then the father's executor after his death, then the executor's executor, then after them the sound grandfather even if elevated, then after the grandfather's death his executor, then his executor's executor. Al-Qahistani added: then the ruler by first right, then the judge or his executor. From al-Durr al-Mukhtar: The insane person who understands sale is permitted by the father, executor, and grandfather, not the brother or uncle, and his ruling is the ruling of the minor. Then the judge or his executor: He only said 'his executor' in the first two, and 'his executor' in the last because the father's executor is the one he appointed after his death to dispose of his son's wealth, whereas the one who permitted him to dispose during his life is an agent, not an executor, and similarly for the grandfather. The judge's executor is the one he ordered to dispose of the orphan's wealth, so he disposes during the judge's life, and he is called an executor even though executorship is succession after death, because here he becomes the father's successor, as if the father made him an executor, so what the judge does becomes as if he did it. So the meaning is: his guardian is his father, then his executor after his death, then the grandfather if the father and his executor are absent, then his executor after his death, then the judge or his executor, whichever disposed is valid. And if he acknowledges regarding his earnings or inheritance with him, it is valid, because when the master permits the minor to trade, his acknowledgment of his earnings is valid because it is part of trade, since if his acknowledgment were not valid, people would not deal with him, even though the guardian's acknowledgment is not valid, because it is an acknowledgment on behalf of another, and the minor's acknowledgment is an acknowledgment against himself. And in Radd al-Muhtar: The ruling of the insane is the ruling of the minor if he reached puberty insane, but if he reached puberty sane then became insane, guardianship does not return to the father by analogy, but to the judge or ruler, and in istihsan: it returns to him. It is said: the first is Abu Yusuf's view, and the second is Muhammad's view, and it is said: the first is Zufar's view, and the second is the view of our three imams. As in al-Tatarkhaniyya. He said: Then the judge or his executor... etc. As for the mother or the mother's executor, they cannot permit him to trade because they are not guardians in transactions absolutely, but are like strangers except regarding preservation; for this reason he does not own the sale of his real estate, and the sale of the mother's executor of the goods that the minor inherited from the mother is permitted by way of strengthening and preservation for the deceased mother, and for the minor, not because it is trade, so if he buys something else for the orphan it is not permissible, and there is no strengthening or preservation in permission. From al-Kifaya. He said: His acknowledgment of his earnings is valid, whether it is an asset or a debt to his guardian or others. He said: Even though the guardian's acknowledgment is not valid... etc.; an indication of what might be objected to his statement.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is an expansion on the conditions and guardianship for a minor to be authorized (ma'dhun) for trade. The author first states the condition: the minor must be capable of understanding that sale removes ownership and purchase brings it. This is a cognitive condition, not merely knowing words. Then the hierarchy of guardians who can grant permission is given: father, his executor, grandfather, his executor, then the judge or his executor. The commentary clarifies that the 'executor' of the father is appointed after death, while a person authorized during life is an agent. For the judge, his 'executor' acts under his authority during his life. The text then presents a proof (lana) that the minor can be authorized because the transaction issues from a capable person with legitimate guardianship, and minorhood is a restriction due to lack of guidance, not an inherent bar. Permission and continuing guardianship allow for benefit. Divorce and manumission are pure harm, so not permitted. Pure benefit (like accepting gifts) is permitted before permission. Sale and purchase are mixed, so only after permission, though prior transactions are suspended. Next, the ruling on acknowledgment: if a minor acknowledges debt or property related to his trade earnings or inheritance, it is valid. This is necessary for trade to function; otherwise people would not deal with him. The guardian's acknowledgment is invalid because it is on behalf of another. The passage ends with an intra-Hanafi dispute: if a person reaches puberty sane then becomes insane, does guardianship return to the father? By analogy (qiyas) it goes to the judge; by istihsan it returns to the father. This is reported as a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, or between Zufar and the three imams. The mufta bihi position is not explicitly given here, but later texts may prefer the istihsan view. This passage exemplifies the Hanafi method of combining logical deduction (qiyas) with preference (istihsan) and the importance of understanding (ta'qul) for legal capacity.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Acknowledgment by the authorized minor of a debt or property related to his trade earnings or inheritance; it is valid and binding on him.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning used in the proof to argue that a permissible transaction from a capable person with lawful guardianship must be executed.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in certain cases, used here to argue that guardianship returns to the father due to maslaha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is an authorized minor's acknowledgment of a trade debt valid?
A) Because the guardian's permission makes the minor an adult.
B) Because it is part of trade; otherwise people would not deal with him.
C) Because the guardian is also bound by the acknowledgment.
D) Because the minor must always be truthful.

Key Takeaway
The authorized minor's transaction is valid by proof, his acknowledgment is binding for trade necessity, and the return of guardianship after insanity is settled by istihsan preferring the father.

Valuation Date for Non-Fungible Usurped Property: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on valuation date

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the valuation date for non-fungible usurped goods and evaluate their respective proofs.

Core Idea
The valuation date for compensation of a unique usurped item differs among Hanafi imams; each based on when the obligation crystallizes.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the value of a non-fungible (unique) usurped item is assessed at the day of usurpation, the day of inability to obtain a like, or the day of litigation. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi jurists balance the cause of liability with the practical ability to determine value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Locate the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the valuation date for a non-fungible usurped item.
Each imam chooses a different day: day of usurpation, day of litigation, or day of inability to obtain a like.
2
Extract the reasoning for each
For each imam, find the legal principle (dalil aqli) that justifies their chosen date.
E.g., Abu Hanifa: the cause (ghasb) obligates value from that day. Muhammad: the obligation is the like, so transfer to value occurs only when the like is unavailable.
3
Note the commentator's preference
The commentator (in 'Umdat al-Ri'aya) favors the day of litigation. Identify his criticisms of the other views.
He argues that the day of litigation is more just because the owner's claim arises only then, and the day of inability is not fixed.
4
Understand the thamarah (practical consequence)
Determine how the choice of date affects the compensation amount, especially if the item's value fluctuates.
This ikhtilaf directly impacts the amount owed: if the value rises or falls, different dates yield different sums.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي غير المثلي قيمته يوم غصبه التحق إلى ما لا مثل له ، أقول : هذا أعدلُ إذ لم يبق شيء من نوعه في يوم الخصومة، والقيمة تعتبر بكثرة الرغبات وقلتها، وفي المعدوم هذا متعذر أو متعسر، ويوم الانقطاع لا ضبط له، وأيضاً لم ينتقل إلى القيمة في هذا اليوم، إذ لم يوجد من المالك طلب، وأيضاً عند وجودِ المثل لم ينتقل إلى القيمة، وعند عدمِهِ لا قيمة له.
(وفي غير المثلي"" قيمته يوم غصبه وحيث لم يجبر فهم منه أنه إنّما ينتقل إلى القيمة بقضاء القاضي فيعتبر قيمته يوم الخصومة والقضاء بخلاف ما لا مثل له ؛ لأنه مطالب بالقيمة بأصل السبب كما وجد ، فيعتبر قيمته عند ذلك.

قال في رد المحتار) : هذا في الهلاك كما هو فرض المسألة، أما إذا استهلكت فكذلك عنده، وعندهما يوم الاستهلاك ، وفي «جامع الفصولين»: غصب شاةً فسمنت ثم ذبحها، ضمن قيمتها يوم غصب لا يوم ذبحه عنده ، وعندهما يوم ذبحه، ولو تلفت بلا إهلاكه ضمن قيمتها يوم غصب.
And for non-fungible items, its value is on the day of its usurpation if it is similar to that which has no like. I say: this is more just because nothing of its type remains on the day of litigation, and value is considered by abundance or scarcity of demand, and for the non-existent this is impossible or difficult, and the day of inability is not fixed. Also, it did not transfer to value on that day since no claim from the owner existed. Also, when the like exists, it does not transfer to value, and when it does not exist, it has no value.
(And for non-fungible items, its value on the day of usurpation and where it is not forced, it is understood that it only transfers to value by the judge's ruling, so its value is considered on the day of litigation and judgment, unlike that which has no like; because he is claimed for value by the original cause as it occurred, so its value is considered at that time.
According to Muhammad, its value is due on the day of inability because the obligated is the like in the liability, and it transfers to value only by inability, so its value is considered on the day of inability. According to Abu Yusuf, the cause (the usurpation) is established for him; because when it became impossible to return, it became like that which has no like, so its value is considered on the day of the cause, since it is the obligator. This is the essence of what is in al-Kifayah.)

Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the valuation date for compensation of non-fungible (غير مثلي) usurped property. The base ruling states that for non-fungible items, the value is assessed on the day of usurpation. The commentator first offers his own opinion, favoring the view that the valuation should be on the day of litigation, because on the day of usurpation the specific item might have perished and no claim existed. He then presents the established opinions from al-Kifayah: According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, the valuation is on the day the owner becomes unable to obtain the like (يوم الانقطاع), because the obligated item is the like in the liability, and only when the like is unavailable does the obligation shift to value. According to Abu Yusuf, the valuation is on the day of usurpation (the cause), because once the item is impossible to return, it is treated as if it had no like, so the cause (usurpation) obligates value from the beginning. The commentator then explains that the statement "I say" indicates he chooses the second opinion (valuation on litigation day), and he provides responses to the arguments of the leading imam (Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad. The ruling in al-Kifayah is also noted. Finally, a quote from Radd al-Muhtar clarifies that the ruling applies to loss (hulak), but if the item is consumed (istihlak), the valuation differs: at Abu Hanifa it is still day of usurpation, while at the two companions it is day of consumption. Examples from Jami' al-Fusulayn illustrate with a sheep: if the usurper fattens and slaughters it, compensation value is day of usurpation according to Abu Hanifa, but day of slaughter according to the two companions.

Key Terms
غير مثلي (ghayr mithli): Property that does not have an exact like (mithl) in the market, e.g., unique items; compensation is by value (qimah).
يوم الغصب (yawm al-ghasb): The day on which the usurpation (ghasb) occurred. One of the proposed dates for valuation.
يوم الانقطاع (yawm al-inqita'): The day on which the owner becomes unable to obtain the like (mithl) of the usurped item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator in the passage, which day does he consider 'more just' for valuation?
A) Day of usurpation
B) Day of inability
C) Day of litigation
D) Day of consumption

Key Takeaway
The valuation date for non-fungible usurped items is disputed among the Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf prefer the day of usurpation, Muhammad prefers the day of inability, and some later commentators prefer the day of litigation; the mufta bihi for loss is the day of usurpation, and for consumption, the day of consumption.

Definition of 'Adadi Mutafawit and Ruling on Returning the Usurped Item
Defining numerically varied items and stating the obligation to return the actual usurped item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'adadi mutafawit, distinguish it from 'adadi mutaqarib, and state the primary obligation of returning the usurped item if still extant.

Core Idea
If the usurped item still exists, it must be returned; paying value is only a substitute when return is impossible.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi classification of usurped items into numerically varied ('adadi mutafawit) and numerically close ('adadi mutaqarib), and then explains the fundamental rule: the primary obligation of a usurper is to return the very item taken, as long as it remains extant. The discussion includes intra-madhhab differences on when value is assessed and whether the primary obligation is the item itself or its value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of the usurped item
Determine whether the item is 'adadi mutafawit (numerically varied, e.g., animals, clothes, fruits) or 'adadi mutaqarib (numerically close, e.g., walnuts, eggs). This classification determines the method of compensation if the item is lost.
The text defines 'adadi mutafawit as items that are counted but whose individuals vary significantly in value.
2
Determine compensation for lost 'adadi mutafawit
If the usurped item is 'adadi mutafawit and is lost or consumed, the usurper must pay its value (qimah), not provide a like (mithl). The day of valuation is disputed: Abu Hanifa says the day of usurpation; the Sahibayn say the day of the act causing loss (e.g., slaughter).
For 'adadi mutaqarib, the compensation is a like (mithl) because individual units are nearly identical.
3
Apply the rule for the extant item
As long as the usurped item remains extant (qa'im), the usurper must return the exact item ('ayn) to its owner. This is wajib based on the hadith 'ala al-yad ma akhadhat hatta tarudd.
The primary obligation is the return of the item itself; paying value is a secondary substitute (khalaf).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the primary obligation
The majority holds that return of the item is the primary obligation; a minority holds that the value is primary and return of the item is a substitute. The mufta bihi position is that return of the item is primary.
The place of return must be the place of usurpation because values vary by location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كالعددي المتفاوت) : أي الشَّيءُ الذي يعدّ، ويكون أفراده متفاوتة، ولا يراد هاهنا ما يقابلُ بالشَّمنِ مبنياً على العدد : كالحيوان مثلاً ، فإنَّه يعد عند البيع من غيرِ أن يقال : يباع الغنم عشرة بكذا.
ثم ذبحها، ضمن قيمتها يوم غصب لا يوم ذبحه عنده ، وعندهما يوم ذبحه، ولو تلفت بلا إهلاكه ضمن قيمتها يوم غصب.
[١] قوله : كالعددي المتفاوت ؛ مثل الدوّاب والثياب، وكالرمان والسفرجل والبطيخ، أما العددي المتقارب : كالجوز والبيض فهو كالمكيل، حتى يجب مثلُه ؛ لقلة التفاوت، وفي البر المخلوط بالشعير القيمة ؛ لأنه لا مثل له، هذا كله فيما هلك المغصوب في يد الغاصب.
أما ما دام قائماً فعليه رد العين المغصوبة، كما قال المصنف له قبيل هذا بقوله : ورد العين قائمة ؛ لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : على اليد ما أخذت حتى تردّ)، وقال: «لا يحل لأحد أن يأخذ متاعَ أخيه لاعباً ولا جاداً، فإن أخذه فليرده عليه).
ولأنَّ اليد حق مقصود، وقد فوّتها عليه، فيجب إعادتها بالردّ إليه، وهو الموجب الأصلي على ما قالوا ، وردّ القيمة مخلص خلفاً ؛ لأنه قاصر، إذ الكمال في ردّ العين و المالية.
وقيل : الموجب الأصلي القيمة، ورد العين مخلص، ويظهر ذلك في بعض الأحكام، والواجب الرد في المكان الذي غصبه فيه ؛ لتفاوت القيم بتفاوتِ الأماكن. كذا في «الهداية»(۳).
('Adadi mutafawit): that which is counted and whose individuals are varied. It is not meant here what is sold by weight based on counting, like animals, for example: they are counted at sale without saying "sheep are sold ten for such-and-such." Then if he slaughters it, he is liable for its value on the day of usurpation, not the day of slaughter according to him (Abu Hanifa), and according to both of them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is the day of slaughter, and if it perishes without his destroying it, he is liable for its value on the day of usurpation.
[The commentator says:] His statement: "like 'adadi mutafawit" includes examples: beasts of burden, clothes, pomegranates, quince, watermelon. As for 'adadi mutaqarib (numerically close) like walnuts and eggs, it is like measured things, so its like must be given due to slight variation. And in wheat mixed with barley, the value is due because it has no like. All this is regarding what perishes in the hand of the usurper.
But as long as it remains extant, he must return the usurped item itself, as the author said previously: "and return the item while it is extant" due to his (ﷺ) saying: "The hand must return what it has taken until it returns it," and he said: "It is not permissible for anyone to take his brother's property in jest or in earnest; if he takes it, let him return it to him." And because the possession is a right intended, and he has deprived him of it, so he must restore it by returning it, which is the primary obligation according to them; paying value is secondary substitution because it is deficient, for perfection lies in returning the item and the value.
And it is said: the primary obligation is the value, and returning the item is a substitution, and this appears in some rulings. And the obligation is to return it in the place where he usurped it, due to variation of values with variation of locations. As in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage defines 'عددي متفاوت' (numerically varied items) and then discusses the ruling for compensation if such an item is usurped and lost or consumed. The commentator explains that 'عددي متفاوت' refers to items that are counted in sale but whose individual members are varied (e.g., animals, clothes, fruits). This contrasts with 'عددي متقارب' (numerically close) like walnuts and eggs, which are similar to measured items (makil) and thus require the return of a like (mithl) due to minimal variation. For mixed items like wheat and barley, value is imposed because there is no like. The passage then shifts to a general rule: if the usurped item is still extant (qa'im), the usurper must return the very item ('ayn) to its owner. This obligation is based on the hadith: "The hand must return what it has taken until it returns it" and another hadith forbidding taking a brother's property. The primary obligation is to return the item itself; paying value is only a substitute when return is impossible. However, there is an alternative view that the primary obligation is value, and returning the item is a substitute. The place of return must be the place of usurpation because values vary by location.

Key Terms
عددي متفاوت (adadi mutafawit): Items that are sold by count but whose individuals vary significantly in value, such as animals, clothes, fruits.
رد العين (radd al-'ayn): Returning the specific usurped item itself to the owner.
مثل (mithl): A similar item that is considered equivalent in kind and quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary obligation for a usurper if the item is still extant?
A) Pay its value
B) Return a similar item (mithl)
C) Return the exact item (al-'ayn)
D) Pay double the value

Key Takeaway
A usurper must return the exact usurped item if it still exists; if lost, compensation depends on whether the item is 'adadi mutafawit (value) or 'adadi mutaqarib (like).

Sale and Guarantee of Musical Instruments: The Hanafi Intra-school Dispute
States the ruling and defines items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal value (taqawwum) of musical instruments and intoxicating drinks, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi is that musical instruments have no legal value — their sale is invalid and destruction requires no compensation.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents a classic dispute within the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that musical instruments (ma'azif) and similar items have legal value (taqawwum), so their sale is valid and destruction requires compensation. His two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), disagree, arguing that such items are primarily used for haram and are thus valueless. The text defines key terms and concludes that the fatwa follows the Sahibayn due to widespread corruption.

Guided Path
1
State the position of Abu Hanifa
Identify the ruling in the matn: guarantee applies and sale is valid for mi'zaf, sukr, and munasif. This is Abu Hanifa's view.
He considers these items to be valuable property (mal mutaqawwim).
2
Identify the Sahibayn's opposing view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that no guarantee applies because the items lack value (la taqawwum). Their reasoning is based on primary use in haram.
The text says 'عندهما لا يضمن حق التقوم' – according to them, he does not guarantee due to value.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof (qiyas)
They argue: the craft (industry) is the original; if the craft is destroyed, no guarantee applies. The instrument is subsidiary to the craft, so likewise no guarantee. This is a qiyas based on the asl (craft) and its hukm.
The text: 'ثم الأصلُ وهو الصنعة لا يجب عليه الضمان بالإتلاف، فكذا التبع'
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, one must pay compensation for destroying such items; under Sahibayn, no compensation. Sale contracts are valid/invalid accordingly.
This affects transactions and liability in daily life.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and tarjih authority
The commentary cites al-Multaqa and Durar al-Hukkam that the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view due to kathrat al-fasad (prevalence of corruption).
Thus, the operative ruling is that sale is invalid and no guarantee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وضمن بكسر ،معزف، وإراقة سكر، ومنصف، وصح بيعها
ولا قيمة له ، والضمان يتبع التقوم ، لكن العين إذا كانت باقياً لا يشترط. وضَمِينَ بكسرِ مِعْزَفِ، وإراقة سكر، ومنصف، وصحٌ بيعُ المعزف : آلة اللهو كالطنبور (۳) والمزمار ونحوهما ، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة ، وعندهما لا يضمن حق التقوم ، ثم الأصلُ وهو الصنعة لا يجب عليه الضمان بالإتلاف، فكذا التبع، فصار كما إذا هلك من غير صنعه.
[٢] قوله : المعزف ; - بكسر الميم وسكون العين المهملة، وفتح الـزاء المعجمة – ، ما ذكره الشارح .
والإراقة : الصب والإسالة.
والسكر : - بفتحتي السين المهملة، والكاف المخففة، والراء المهملة - : النيء من ماء الرطب إذا اشتد.
والمنصف - بفتح الصاد المهملة المشددة - : ما ذهب نصفه بالطبخ. كذا في «الهداية»(4) و«الصحاح )
And he guarantees with a broken [kasra] of a musical instrument, and spilling of an intoxicating drink, and half-cooked, and its sale is valid.
And it has no value, and guarantee follows value, but the substance if it remains does not require [guarantee]. And the guarantee with a broken musical instrument, and spilling of intoxicating drink, and half-cooked, and the sale of the musical instrument is valid: it is an instrument of amusement like the tanbur and flute and similar. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does not guarantee due to value. Then the original, which is the craft, does not necessitate guarantee upon destruction, so likewise the subsidiary, so it becomes as if it perished without his action.
[2] He said: al-mi'zaf - with a kasra on the meem, sukoon on the ain, and fatha on the zay - is what the commentator mentioned.
And al-iraqah: pouring and flowing.
And al-sukr: with two fatha on the seen, lightened kaf, and ra with fatha: the raw liquid of fresh dates when it becomes strong.
And al-munasif: with shadda on the sad with fatha: that which has lost half by cooking. So in al-Hidayah and al-Sihah.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on the guarantee and sale of musical instruments (ma'azif) and related items like spilled wine and half-cooked date juice. The matn states that if someone breaks a musical instrument or spills intoxicating drink or destroys half-cooked juice, he guarantees it, and the sale of these items is valid according to Abu Hanifa. The commentary explains that according to Abu Hanifa, these items have value (taqawwum) even though they may be used for prohibited purposes. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that such items do not have value (la taqawwum) because they are primarily used for haram, so there is no guarantee. The principle discussed: guarantee follows value; if the substance (ayn) remains, the ruler's guarantee is not affected, but the value matters. The commentary then defines the terms: mi'zaf is a musical instrument like tanbur and flute; iraqah is pouring/spilling; sukr is raw fresh date juice when it becomes strong (i.e., intoxicating); munasif is date juice that has lost half by cooking (i.e., reduced by half). The text notes that the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is that the sale is not valid, and the fatwa is upon that due to widespread corruption.

Key Terms
المعزف (al-mi'zaf): A musical instrument, specifically stringed instruments like the tanbur, and also wind instruments like the flute.
السكر (al-sukr): Raw date juice that has become strong (i.e., intoxicating), not yet fully cooked.
المنصف (al-munasif): Date juice that has been cooked until half of it evaporates; it is still potentially intoxicating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, according to Abu Hanifa
B) No, according to Sahibayn and the mufta bihi
C) Yes, for tanbur but not for flute
D) Only if sold for lawful use

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that musical instruments and similar items have no legal value, so their sale is invalid and destruction does not require compensation.

Definition and Evidence of Shuf'a (Pre-emption)
Opening of Shuf'a chapter with definition and hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define shuf'a according to the Hanafi school and cite the textual evidence that establishes it.

Core Idea
Shuf'a is the right to take over sold real estate, proven by multiple sound hadith.

This passage opens the chapter on Pre-emption (Shuf'a). It provides both a linguistic and legal definition, drawing a parallel with the prohibition of ghasb (usurpation) to highlight the unique Shari'ah validation of this right. The primary evidence comes from several authentic hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and the four Sunan, each emphasizing the right of a neighbor or co-owner to claim property before an outsider. Understanding these proofs is essential for grasping the scope and application of pre-emption in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic and legal definition
Read the definition: 'Shuf'a is the ownership of real estate.' Note the linguistic root shaf' meaning joining, and the legal meaning as a right to take over sold property.
The definition explicitly limits shuf'a to real estate ('aqar), not movables except as subsidiaries.
2
Analyze the parallel with ghasb
The commentator notes a similarity to ghasb (usurpation): both involve taking another's property without consent. However, shuf'a is legalized by Shari'ah, while ghasb is forbidden.
This helps appreciate that shuf'a is an exception to the general prohibition of taking property without owner's consent.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Four hadith are cited. Identify each: (1) Bukhari: 'The neighbor has more right to his pre-emption'; (2) Muslim: 'The Prophet decreed shuf'a in every undivided shared property'; (3) Abu Dawud: 'The neighbor has more right to the house or land'; (4) Sunan: 'The neighbor has more right to his pre-emption, to be awaited even if absent, if they share a pathway.'
The hadith collectively establish the right for co-owners and neighbors with a common pathway.
4
Recognize the limitation to real estate
The passage stresses that shuf'a applies only to immovable property ('aqar) like houses, land, vineyards, mills, wells. Movable items like trees and buildings only fall under shuf'a as subsidiaries attached to real estate.
This distinction is crucial for correct application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة) هي تملك عقار [٢] قوله : كتاب الشفعة ... الخ ؛ الشفعة بالضم، بمعنى المفعول، وهي الشفع بالفتح ، بمعنى الضمّ، وسُمِّيت بها لما فيها من ضم المشتراة : يعني العقار، والمناسبة بينها وبين الغصب تملك الإنسان مال غيره بلا رضاء في كل منهما. والأصل في ثبوتِ الشفعة ما أخرجه البخاري في «صحيحه»: عـن عمـرو بـن الشريد عن أبي رافع مولى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : «الجار أحق بسقبه، قيل لعمرو بن الشريد (1) : ما السقب؟ قال : الجوار». وما أخرجه مسلم في صحيحه عن جابر ، قال : «قضى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالشفعة في كل مشترك لم يقسم ربعة أو حائط). وما أخرجه أبو داود إنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : «جار الدار أحق بدار الجار أو الأرض» (۳). وما أخرجه أصحاب السنن الأربع عن جابر الله قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «الجار (٤) أحق بشفعته ينتظر بها، وإن كان غائباً إذا كان طريقهما واحدا ، هذا ما استدل أصحابنا . [٢] قوله : هي : تملك عقار ؛ دون المنقول ؛ كالشجر والبناء، فإنّه منقول لم تجب الشفعة إلا بتبعيته، والعقار كالدار، والكرم والرحى والبئر، والصيغة من باب التفعيل، يعني مالك شدن زمین را «فوائد عارفیة).
The Book of Shuf'a: It is the ownership of real estate. [2] His saying: The Book of Shuf'a... etc. Shuf'a (with damm) is in the sense of the passive participle, and it is from shaf' (with fatha) meaning joining. It is named so because it involves joining the purchased property, i.e., real estate. The connection between it and ghasb is that each involves owning another's property without consent. The evidential basis for establishing shuf'a includes what Bukhari narrated in his Sahih from 'Amr ibn al-Sharid from Abu Rafi'... 'The neighbor has more right to his pre-emption.' And what Muslim narrated in his Sahih from Jabir... 'The Messenger of Allah decreed pre-emption in every shared property that has not been divided, whether it is a dwelling or a garden.' And what Abu Dawud narrated... 'The neighbor of a house has more right to the house or land.' And what the authors of the four Sunan narrated from Jabir... 'The neighbor has more right to his pre-emption; he should wait for it even if he is absent, if their pathway is one.' This is what our companions used as evidence. [2] His saying: It is ownership of real estate, not movable property like trees and buildings, for that is movable and pre-emption is not obligatory except as a subsidiary. Real estate includes house, vineyard, mill, well. The form is from the pattern taf'il, meaning 'to become owner of land' (as per Fawa'id 'Arifiyyah).
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This is the opening of the chapter on Pre-emption (Shuf'a). The author defines shuf'a as 'the ownership of real estate' and notes the linguistic connection: shuf'a comes from shaf' (joining). The commentator highlights the similarity between shuf'a and ghasb: both involve owning another's property without their consent, but shuf'a is legalized by Shari'ah. The evidence for shuf'a is four hadith: (1) from Bukhari: 'The neighbor has more right to his pre-emption' (sabqah means right of proximity); (2) from Muslim: 'The Prophet decreed shuf'a in every undivided shared property'; (3) from Abu Dawud: 'The neighbor of a house has more right to the house or land'; (4) from the four Sunan: 'The neighbor has more right to his pre-emption, to be awaited even if absent, if they share a pathway.' The commentator clarifies that shuf'a applies only to real estate ('aqar), not movable property (manqul) except as a subsidiary. Examples of real estate: house, vineyard, mill, well.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf‘ah): The right of pre-emption enabling a neighbor or co-owner to take over real estate sold to a third party.
العقار (al-‘aqār): Immovable property such as houses, land, vineyards, wells, and mills.
المنقول (al-manqūl): Movable property such as trees and buildings that are not permanently attached; shuf'a does not apply to them directly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only real estate ('aqar), not movable property except as subsidiary.
D) Only land, not buildings.

Key Takeaway
Shuf'a is a Shari'ah-granted right attached to real estate, supported by multiple prophetic traditions.

Definition of Shuf'a and the Nature of Its Obligation
Defining shuf'a and explaining the technical meaning of wujub

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define shuf'a and explain why the term 'wajib' in 'tajibu ba'da al-bay' means confirmation (thubut) rather than a sin-bearing obligation.

Core Idea
Shuf'a is the right to forcibly take a partner's sold share; its 'obligation' is establishment, not religious duty.

The commentator opens the Book of Shuf'a by defining it as the forced purchase of a property from its new buyer for the same price. A critical nuance is that the word 'wajib' here does not carry the usual fiqh sense of a duty whose omission is sinful. Instead, it indicates that the right is confirmed upon the occurrence of the cause—namely the sale of a jointly-owned property. This lesson unpacks the definition and the special usage of wujub in shuf'a.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
Read the opening line: 'shuf'a is to own the property from its buyer forcibly for the equivalent of its price.' Mark the key elements: ownership, buyer, forcible, equivalent price.
The definition is taken from the matn of al-Wiqaya.
2
Recognise the exclusions
The commentary notes that shuf'a does not apply to properties acquired without compensation (gift, inheritance, charity) or where the compensation is not specific currency (dower, rental, khul'). List these excluded transactions.
This is a crucial limitation: only sales (or transactions in the meaning of sale) trigger shuf'a.
3
Clarify the meaning of 'wajib'
The commentator explicitly says: 'al-murad bi al-wujub al-thubut'. Understand that 'tajibu ba'da al-bay' means the right is established after the sale, not that the pre-emptor is religiously obligated to claim it.
This resolves a common misunderstanding. The right exists, but the shafi' may choose not to exercise it without sin.
4
Understand the role of ishhad
The right is initially unstable; it becomes stable only after the shafi' takes witnesses (ishhad) to his demand. Without ishhad, any delay in claiming voids the right.
Witnesses serve to confirm the claim and prevent denial by the buyer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الاتصال. قوله : بعد البيع ... الخ ؛ وكذا تثبت الشفعة بعد ما في معنى البيع : كالصلح على مال، والهبة بعوض. كذا في «شرح المجمع». قوله : بالإشهاد ؛ قال في «البحر» : فإذا أخبر بحضرة شهود يشهدهم عليه ، وإن لم يكن بحضرته أحدٌ يطلب من غير إشهاد ، والإشهاد لمخالفة الجحود، والطلب لا بد منه كيلا يسقط حقه فيما بينه وبين الله ، ولتمكنه من الحلف إذا حلف ؛ ولئلا يكون معرضاً عنها وراضياً، وكون الطلب متصلاً يعني على الفور، هذا عند عامة المشايخ. وروى هشام عن محمد إنّ له التأمل إلى آخر المجلس، كالمخير ؛ لأنه تملك ، ولا بد من التأمل، وهو اختيار الكرخي ، وبعض المشايخ ، وفي «التجريد»: وهو أصح الروايتين. وتملك بالأخذ بالتراضي، أو بقضاء القاضي بقدر رؤوس الشفعاء لا الملك للخليط في نفس المبيع. وتملك بالأخذ بالتراضي، أو بقضاء القاضي بقدرِ رؤوس الشفعاء" لا الملك) (۱) : أي إنما يملك العقار إذا أخذهُ الشَّفيعُ برضاه، وبرضا المشتري، وقوله : أو بقضاء القاضي ؛ عطف على الأخذ لا على التراضي ؛ لأنَّ القاضي إذا حَكَمَ يثبت الملك للشفيع قبل أخذه، (للخليط في نفس المبيع. قوله : وتملك بالأخذ بالتراضي ... الخ ؛ على صيغة المجهول، والضمير راجع إلى العقار، والمراد بالتراضي رضاء البائع والمشتري والشفيع، فإذا تبقى واحد منها لم يملك بالأخذ إذا سلّمها المشتري أو حكم الحاكم ؛ لأنَّ ملك المشتري قد تم، فلا ينتقل إلى الشفيع إلا بالتراضي، أو قضاء القاضي، ويظهرُ فائدة هذا الأخذ إذا سلّمها أو قضى القاضي بها فيما إذا مات الشفيع بعد الطلبين، أعني الإشهاد والمواثبة، وتمام الكلام في «الهداية». فانظر هنا، وفائدة توقف الملك بتسليم المشتري إلى وقتِ حكم الحاكم أن يثبت الملك للشفيع، وإن وجد منه الطلبان، أما تسليم المشتري بدون حكم الحاكم أو بحكم الحاكم، فإذا وجد أحدهما حينئذ تملك الشفيع الدار المشفوعة. قوله : بقدر رؤوس الشفعاء ... الخ ؛ أي بقدرِ رؤوس الشفعاء الجار فيه. قوله : للخليط ... الخ ؛ متعلّق يجب ؛ أي يجب الشفعة للخليط، ويقسم على عدد الرؤوس إذا كانوا أكثر، لا بقدر الملك ؛ لأنهم استووا في سبب الاستحقاق ؛ لوجودِ علّة استحقاق الكلّ في حق كلّ واحدٍ منهم ؛ ولهذا لو انفرد واحد منهم أخذ الكل، والاستواء في العلة يوجب الاستواء في الحكم، ولا يرجح بكثرة العلل بل بقوة فيها. (۱) لاستواء الكلّ ؛ لوجود علّته فيجب الاستواء في الحكم وشمل ما لو كان المشتري أحدهم، وطلب معهم، فيحسب واحداً منهم، ويقسم المبيع بينهم. ينظر : «رد المحتار»(٥: ١٣٩).
The Book of Shuf'a: its definition, types, and rulings. [It is] to own the property from its buyer forcibly for the equivalent of its price, and it becomes obligatory after the sale, and it becomes established by taking witnesses. 'Upon its buyer forcibly for the equivalent of it': i.e., the equivalent of the price of the purchased property, which is the price with which it was purchased. 'And it becomes obligatory after the sale': the intended meaning of obligation is confirmation. 'And it becomes established by taking witnesses': because the right of shuf'a before taking witnesses is unstable; because if he delays in the demand, it becomes void. So when he takes witnesses, it becomes established: i.e., it does not become void thereafter by delay. His statement: 'upon its buyer' is attached to his statement: 'to own', and this is a caveat against what is owned without compensation: like gift, inheritance, and charity, and compensation that is not an 'ayn (specific item) like dower, rental, and khul', for there is no shuf'a in any of these. So if a land is made as dower for a woman, or she divorces (khul') with it, or he gifts the land, there is no shuf'a. He said 'forcibly' as a restriction, because the buyer does not consent to it, and it distinguishes the attribution of ownership from the doer. This is from 'al-Fawa'id al-'Aarifiyyah'. His statement: 'it becomes obligatory after the sale... etc.': the intended meaning of obligation is confirmation, as the commentator said. He said this to indicate that the intended meaning is not the technical obligation whose abandonment incurs sin. So the meaning is that it is established when its cause is realized, not that the intention is the necessity of sin by leaving it. He only said 'after the sale' because its cause is connection (with the property). His statement: 'after the sale... etc.': similarly, shuf'a is established after what is in the meaning of a sale: like a settlement for property, and a gift for compensation. This is from 'Sharh al-Majma''. His statement: 'by taking witnesses': He said in 'al-Bahr': So if he informs in the presence of witnesses whom he makes witness upon him, and if there is no one present, he demands without witnesses, and the witnesses are for refuting denial. The demand is necessary so that his right does not lapse between him and Allah, and for him to be able to take an oath if he swears, and so that he is not considered to be turning away from it and being pleased. And the demand being immediate means it must be at once; this is according to the generality of the mashayikh. And Hisham narrated from Muhammad that he may deliberate until the end of the gathering, like the option of choice, because it is ownership, and deliberation is necessary. This is the choice of al-Karkhi and some mashayikh, and in 'al-Tajrid': it is the more authentic of the two narrations. 'And he owns by taking with mutual consent, or by the judge's decree, according to the number of pre-emptors, not ownership for the partner in the actual sold property.' 'And he owns by taking with mutual consent, or by the judge's decree according to the number of pre-emptors' not ownership: i.e., the pre-emptor only owns the property if he takes it with his consent and the consent of the buyer. His statement 'or by the judge's decree' is conjoined to 'taking', not to 'mutual consent', because when the judge judges, ownership is established for the pre-emptor before his taking. 'For the partner in the actual sold property': His statement 'And he owns by taking with mutual consent... etc.' is in the passive voice, and the pronoun refers to the property. The intended meaning of mutual consent is the consent of the seller, buyer, and pre-emptor. So if one of them remains, he does not own by taking unless the buyer hands it over or the judge judges, because the ownership of the buyer is complete, so it does not transfer to the pre-emptor except by mutual consent or the judge's decree. The benefit of this taking appears if the buyer hands it over or the judge judges regarding it in the case where the pre-emptor dies after the two demands, namely taking witnesses and prompt demand. The full discussion is in 'al-Hidayah', so refer there. The benefit of the ownership being contingent on the buyer's delivery until the time of the judge's ruling is that ownership is established for the pre-emptor even if he made the two demands. As for the buyer's delivery without the judge's ruling or with his ruling, if either occurs then the pre-emptor owns the pre-empted house. His statement 'according to the number of pre-emptors... etc.': i.e., according to the number of pre-emptors who are partners in it. His statement 'for the partner in the actual sold property... etc.' is attached to 'it becomes obligatory': i.e., shuf'a is obligatory for the partner, and it is divided according to the number of heads if there are more than one, not according to the amount of ownership, because they are equal in the cause of entitlement due to the existence of the cause of entitlement for all in respect of each one of them. Hence if one of them alone takes, he takes the whole. Equality in the cause necessitates equality in the ruling, and it is not weighed by multiplicity of causes but by strength in it. (1) For the equality of all due to the existence of the cause, so equality in the ruling is necessary. This includes the case where the buyer is one of them and demands with them, so he is counted as one of them and the sold property is divided among them. See: 'Radd al-Muhtar' (5:139).
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the Book of Shuf'a (pre-emption) from the commentary on Al-Wiqaya. It defines shuf'a as the right to compulsorily take ownership of property from its buyer for the same price he paid, after the sale is concluded. The word 'obligatory' here means 'established' (thubut), not the technical obligation that incurs sin if abandoned. The right is initially unstable and becomes stable only after the pre-emptor (shafi') takes witnesses (ishhad) to his demand. The demand must be immediate (fawr) according to the majority of mashayikh; but Hisham narrated from Imam Muhammad that the shafi' may deliberate until the end of the gathering (like when having a choice). Al-Karkhi and some mashayikh chose this, and in al-Tajrid it is deemed the more authentic narration. Ownership of the pre-empted property is acquired either by mutual consent of seller, buyer, and shafi', or by the judge's decree. The division among multiple shufa' is per capita (according to number of heads), not according to shares of ownership, because the cause (being a partner) is equal for all. If the buyer is also a partner, he is counted as one of them.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): The right of a co-owner to compulsorily purchase the share of a new buyer for the same price, preventing a stranger from becoming a co-owner.
الشفيع (al-shafi'): The person who has the right of pre-emption, typically a co-owner or neighbour.
الإشهاد (al-ishhad): Taking witnesses to the demand of shuf'a to stabilize the right and prevent denial.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Here it means thubut (confirmation/establishment), not the technical obligation that incurs sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is meant by 'tajibu ba'da al-bay' (it becomes obligatory after the sale)?
A) The shafi' is religiously obligated to claim shuf'a immediately, and delay is a sin.
B) The right of shuf'a is established after the sale, not that it is a sin to abandon it.
C) The buyer is obligated to sell to the shafi' at a lower price.
D) The sale is invalid if the shafi' does not claim immediately.

Key Takeaway
Shuf'a is a confirmed right (not a religious duty) that arises from the sale of a jointly-owned property and must be claimed immediately with witnesses.

Definition and Priority Order of Shuf'ah Claimants
Definition and priority of shuf'ah claimants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of shuf'ah and list the three categories of claimants in their order of priority according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is a right of pre-emption for partners and neighbors; the first claim belongs to the partner in the property itself.

Shuf'ah (pre-emption) protects against unwanted third-party intrusion by allowing a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold share. This lesson defines shuf'ah and explains the hierarchical order of claimants as established in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of shuf'ah
From the passage, shuf'ah is the right to take over a sold property by paying its price. Recognize that it applies to three categories of claimants.
The term 'shuf'ah' is derived from the root meaning 'joining' or 'adding'.
2
List the priority order of claimants
The text states: first, the partner in the property itself; second, the partner in a right attached to the property (e.g., water share, private path); third, the adjacent neighbor (jar mulasiq).
The word 'thumma' (then) indicates both the right and the order.
3
Understand what constitutes a 'partner in rights'
Examples given: a water share (shurb) of a river where ships do not sail, and a private path (tariq) that does not lead through. These are rights attached to the property.
These are not full ownership shares but limited rights.
4
Clarify the adjacent neighbor's qualification
The neighbor must be immediately adjacent (mulasiq), even if his door opens onto a different street. The example of placing a beam on the wall is just an illustration, not a condition.
The text emphasizes that even if the neighbor has nothing on the wall, he still qualifies.
5
Note the range of persons eligible
Shuf'ah applies to all types of people: a mukatib (slave under contract of manumission), a ma'dhun (slave permitted to trade), and a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject).
This is based on the general application of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة تعريفها وأنواعها وأحكامها
تم له في حق المبيع كالشرب والطريق الخاصين كشرب نهر لا تَجْري فيه السفن ، وطريق لا ينفذ ، ثُمَّ لجار ملاصق ، بابه في سكة أخرى ، كواضع جذع على الحائط ثم له في حق المبيع) : أي ثُمَّ للشَّريك في حق المبيع : (كالشرب) والطريق الخاصين كشرب نهر لا تجري فيه السفن، وطريق لا ينفذ ، ثُمَّ لجار ملاصق ، بابه في سكة أخرى، كواضع جذع على الحائط) : إِنما ذَكَرَ واضعَ الجذع ليعلم أنَّه جار، وليس بخليط ، ولا يشترط للجار الملاصق وضع الجذع حتى لو لم يكن له شيء على الحائط يكون جاراً ملاصقاً
[1) قوله : ثم ؛ لفظ : ثمّ ؛  يُفيدُ ثبوت حق الشفعة لكل واحد من هؤلاء، وأيضاً يُفيد الترتيب. كذا في «الهداية» [2]قوله : للجار الملاصق ؛ سواء كان مكاتباً أو مأذوناً أو ذميّاً عملاً بإطلاق الحديث، وهو قوله : «الشفعة لشريك لم يقاسم»).
Book of Shuf'ah: its definition, types, and rulings. Then he has right in the sold property like the water share and private paths, like a water share of a river in which ships do not sail, and a path that does not lead through. Then for an adjacent neighbor whose door is in another alley, like one who places a beam on the wall. Then he has right in the sold property: that is, then for the partner in the right to the sold property: like the water share and private paths, like a water share of a river in which ships do not sail, and a path that does not lead through, then for an adjacent neighbor whose door is in another alley, like one who places a beam on the wall. He only mentioned the one placing the beam to indicate that he is a neighbor, not a co-mixer, and it is not a condition for the adjacent neighbor to have placed a beam, so even if he has nothing on the wall, he is an adjacent neighbor. [1) He said: 'Thumma' the word 'thumma' indicates the establishment of the right of shuf'ah for each of these, and also indicates order. Thus in al-Hidayah. [2] He said: For the adjacent neighbor, whether he is a mukatib, or a ma'dhun, or a dhimmi, acting on the general application of the hadith, which is his saying: 'Shuf'ah is for a partner who has not divided.'
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah defines shuf'ah (pre-emption) and lays out the priority order of claimants. The author begins by stating the right of shuf'ah for a partner in the property itself (the sold item), then for a partner in a right attached to the property, such as a water share (shurb) or a private path (tariq) that does not serve as a public thoroughfare. Finally, it extends to an immediately adjacent neighbor (jar mulasiq), even if his door opens onto a different alley. The example of placing a beam on the wall is given to illustrate the type of neighbor who qualifies, but the author clarifies that this is merely an example; the condition of adjacency is sufficient without any beam. The footnotes elaborate: the word 'thumma' indicates both the affirmation of the right for each category and their sequential order. The hadith 'Shuf'ah is for a partner who has not divided' is cited to show the general applicability of shuf'ah to partners, and this right applies to all types of people, including a mukatib (slave under contract of manumission), a ma'dhun (slave permitted to trade), and a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state).

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of a partner or neighbor to take over a sold property by paying its price, protecting against unwanted third-party intrusion.
جار ملاصق (jar mulasiq): An immediately adjacent neighbor whose property touches the sold property, even if their door is on a different street.
ثم (thumma): In this context, indicates both the establishment of the right of shuf'ah for each category and their sequential order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is a right of pre-emption with a clear priority: partner in property, then partner in rights, then adjacent neighbor.
